**Phase 135 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 287 test modules green. Sovereign Wavelet Tree (Grossi, Gupta & Vitter, 2003) ‚ÄĒ a **succinct index over an arbitrary-alphabet sequence** that lifts rank/select from bits to symbols, built directly on the Rank/Select primitive of P134. Distinct symbols are mapped to contiguous ids `[0, ŌÉ)` in sorted order; the root stores one `RankSelect` bitvector marking, per position, whether its id lies in the lower or upper half of the alphabet range, and positions recurse into a left child (lower half) and a right child (upper half), `‚Ćąlog‚āā ŌÉ‚ĆČ` levels deep. With `rank`/`select` on each level it answers, in `O(log ŌÉ)`: `access(i)` (the symbol at `i`), `rank(symbol, i)` (occurrences in `[0, i)`), `select(symbol, k)` (position of the `k`-th `symbol`), `quantile(i, j, k)` (the `k`-th smallest symbol in `[i, j)`), and `range_count(i, j, lo, hi)`. This is the symbol-generalisation of P134's bit rank/select and the backbone of compressed text indexes ‚ÄĒ *exact*, distinct from the frequency *sketches*. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against naive list operations matched all five queries** ‚ÄĒ `access`/`rank`/`select`/`quantile`/`range_count` ‚ÄĒ across 8 configs (ŌÉ = 1, 2, 3, 5, 7, 50, a string alphabet, and a wide/negative integer alphabet), with the identities `access(select(s,k))=s` and `rank(s, select(s,k))=k‚ąí1` holding throughout. Exposed at `/api/v1/wavelet`. Pure stdlib (reusing `RankSelect`); thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static ‚ÄĒ built once from the sequence). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/wavelet_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 135A: `pradyos/core/wavelet_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `WaveletTreeError(detail)`; `WaveletTree(sequence=None)` with `build(sequence)`, `access(i)`, `rank(symbol, i)`, `select(symbol, k)`, `quantile(i, j, k)`, `range_count(i, j, lo, hi)`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `alphabet_size` / `symbols` properties + `stats()`. Symbols must be one orderable kind (`int`/`float` or `str`); bools, non-orderable values and mixed kinds raise `WaveletTreeError`, as do out-of-range indices/ranks. Each node's split bitvector is a P134 `RankSelect`.
- ‚úÖ 135B: `pradyos/web/wavelet_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_wavelet_routes(app, wavelet_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/wavelet/build` (body `{sequence[]}`; 422 on missing / mixed-kind), `GET /api/v1/wavelet/access` (query `?i=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `POST /api/v1/wavelet/rank` (body `{symbol, i}`), `POST /api/v1/wavelet/quantile` (body `{i, j, k}`), `GET /api/v1/wavelet/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/wavelet/reset` (`select` / `range_count` remain on the core class).

Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 135D: `tests/test_wavelet_tree.py` (34) + `tests/test_wavelet_web.py` (22) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against naive** for all five queries across 8 alphabet configs (incl. non-powers-of-two, strings, wide ints); identities (`select`‚ÜĒ`rank`‚ÜĒ`access`); edge cases (empty, ŌÉ=1, ŌÉ=2, single element); validation (mixed kind, bool, non-orderable, out-of-range indices/ranks, `select` overcount, absent symbol ‚Üí rank 0) + `WaveletTreeError.detail`; `range_count` half-open / inverted / full-alphabet; determinism; build replaces; reset; 10-thread concurrent queries; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `rankselect`).

**Phase 136 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 289 test modules green. Sovereign Skew Heap (Sleator & Tarjan, 1986) ‚ÄĒ a **self-adjusting meldable priority queue**, a new capability for the platform (no heap/priority-queue existed) and a thematic companion to the splay tree (both self-adjusting, no balance metadata). The single primitive is **meld**: keep the smaller of the two roots, meld its right subtree with the other heap, then **swap that root's children** ‚ÄĒ the swap is what amortises the right-spine to `O(log n)` with no rank/height bookkeeping. `insert` melds a singleton, `extract_min` melds the root's two children, and `meld` unions two heaps wholesale (the operation an array binary-heap lacks). This implementation melds **iteratively** ‚ÄĒ merging the two ascending right-spines into a sorted list and relinking from the back with the child-swap ‚ÄĒ so it is **immune to Python recursion limits on adversarial inputs**. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against `heapq` over 15 000 interleaved insert/extract ops** matched every `extract_min`; `meld` of two heaps equals the sorted union; and **20 000 ascending (and 20 000 descending) inserts complete with no `RecursionError`**. Exposed at `/api/v1/skewheap`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/skew_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 136A: `pradyos/core/skew_heap.py` ‚ÄĒ `SkewHeapError(detail)`; `SkewHeap()` with `insert(value)` (duplicates allowed), `extract_min()` / `peek_min()` / `find_min()` (raise on empty), `meld(other)` (unions; empties `other`), `keys_sorted()` (read-only), `reset()`, `is_empty()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `kind` properties + `stats()`. Values must be one orderable kind (`int`/`float` or `str`); bools, non-orderable values, mixed-kind inserts and mismatched-kind melds raise `SkewHeapError`. The meld is iterative (no recursion-depth risk).
- ‚úÖ 136B: `pradyos/web/skew_heap_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_skewheap_routes(app, skew_heap=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/skewheap/insert` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / bad / mixed-kind), `POST /api/v1/skewheap/extract_min` (422 on empty), `GET /api/v1/skewheap/peek` (`min` null when empty), `GET /api/v1/skewheap/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/skewheap/reset` (`meld` stays on the core class).
- ‚úÖ 136C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase136.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `skew_heap` param, and a single `register_skewheap_routes(app, skew_heap)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 136D: `tests/test_skew_heap.py` (33) + `tests/test_skewheap_web.py` (19) ‚ÄĒ priority-queue semantics (extract in sorted order, peek, keys_sorted, duplicates, floats, strings); **a differential test against `heapq`** over 15 000 interleaved ops; **adversarial 20 000 ascending & descending inserts** (no recursion error); **meld** (= sorted union, empties other, into/with empty, self-noop, kind-mismatch & non-heap raise); empty-op & validation raises (bool, non-orderable, mixed kind) + `SkewHeapError.detail`; determinism; `kind` resets when emptied; reset; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `wavelet`).
- ‚úÖ 136E: `scripts/prove.py` ‚ÄĒ 289 test modules registered (Phase 136 appends `test_skew_heap.py` + `test_skewheap_web.py`).

**Phase 137 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 291 test modules green. Sovereign Interval Tree (Cormen‚ÄďLeiserson‚ÄďRivest‚ÄďStein, augmented BST) ‚ÄĒ a **dynamic set of intervals supporting overlap and stabbing queries**, a new capability for the platform. Intervals `[low, high]` (endpoints inclusive) are stored in a BST keyed by `low`, and every node is augmented with `max` ‚ÄĒ the maximum `high` endpoint in its subtree ‚ÄĒ which lets a search prune whole subtrees: to find an overlapping interval, descend left when the left subtree's `max` reaches the query's `low`, else right. Supports `insert`, `remove`, `contains`, `overlap_any(low, high)`, `overlap(low, high)` (all intersecting intervals, with subtree-`max` pruning), `stab(point)`, and `count`. Every operation is **iterative** (the augmentation is recomputed along the recorded path), so the tree is immune to recursion limits even on adversarial sorted-`low` inserts. This is *different* from the platform's point-keyed ordered maps (Splay/P133, Treap/P113, Skip List/P78): it answers *range-intersection* queries via the subtree-`max` augmentation. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute-force scan matched `overlap`/`stab`/`overlap_any` over 300 queries**, the **subtree-`max` invariant held through 6 000 random insert/remove ops**, and **15 000 ascending inserts completed with no `RecursionError`** and a correct overlap query. Exposed at `/api/v1/intervaltree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/interval_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 137A: `pradyos/core/interval_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `IntervalTreeError(detail)`; `IntervalTree()` with `insert(low, high)` (duplicates allowed), `remove(low, high)` ‚Üí bool, `contains(low, high)`, `overlap_any(low, high)` ‚Üí `(low,high)`|None, `overlap(low, high)` ‚Üí sorted list, `stab(point)` ‚Üí sorted list, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `max_endpoint` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. Endpoints must be numbers with `low ‚Č§ high` (bools and non-numerics raise `IntervalTreeError`). Insert/remove are iterative with bottom-up `max` fixup along the path; queries prune via subtree-`max`.
- ‚úÖ 137B: `pradyos/web/interval_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_intervaltree_routes(app, interval_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/intervaltree/insert` (body `{low, high}`; 422 on missing / `low>high` / non-numeric), `DELETE /api/v1/intervaltree/remove` (body `{low, high}` ‚Üí `{removed, size}`), `GET /api/v1/intervaltree/overlap` (query `?low=&high=`), `GET /api/v1/intervaltree/stab` (query `?point=`), `GET /api/v1/intervaltree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/intervaltree/reset` (`overlap_any` / `contains` stay on the core class).
- ‚úÖ 137C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase137.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `interval_tree` param, and a single `register_intervaltree_routes(app, interval_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 137D: `tests/test_interval_tree.py` (33) + `tests/test_intervaltree_web.py` (23) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against brute force** for `overlap`/`stab`/`overlap_any` + a 6 000-op random insert/remove sequence holding the **`max`-augmentation invariant**; **adversarial 15 000 sorted inserts** (no recursion error); inclusive-endpoint overlap, single-point & negative intervals, duplicates, `remove` (root / two-children / absent); validation (`low>high`, bool, non-numeric, non-numeric `stab`) + `IntervalTreeError.detail`; reset; `max_endpoint` / height / determinism; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `skewheap`).
- ‚úÖ 137E: `scripts/prove.py` ‚ÄĒ 291 test modules registered (Phase 137 appends `test_interval_tree.py` + `test_intervaltree_web.py`).

**Phase 138 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 293 test modules green. Sovereign Sparse Table (Bender & Farach-Colton) ‚ÄĒ a **static range-minimum/maximum index answering queries in `O(1)`** after `O(n log n)` preprocessing, a new capability for the platform. It precomputes `table[k][i] = aggregate of the 2ŠĶŹ elements starting at i`, so any half-open range `[lo, hi)` is covered by **two overlapping power-of-two blocks** ‚ÄĒ `op(table[k][lo], table[k][hi‚ąí2ŠĶŹ])` with `k = ‚Ćälog‚āā(hi‚ąílo)‚Ćč` ‚ÄĒ a constant-time query, exact because `min`/`max` are **idempotent** (`op(x,x)=x`) so the overlap is harmless. This is *different* from the platform's *dynamic* Segment Tree (P81), which supports updates with `O(log n)` queries: a sparse table is **static** (built once, no updates) but answers in `O(1)`, the right tradeoff for immutable data. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against brute-force `min`/`max` matched every one of the `O(n¬≤)` ranges for both ops across array sizes 1‚Ä¶100**, plus 2 000 random queries on a 5 000-element array. Exposed at `/api/v1/sparsetable`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static ‚ÄĒ built once from the array). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/sparse_table_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 138A: `pradyos/core/sparse_table.py` ‚ÄĒ `SparseTableError(detail)`; `SparseTable(values=None, op="min")` with `build(values, op=None)` (static rebuild), `query(lo, hi)` (half-open `[lo, hi)`, `O(1)`), `get(i)`, `reset(op=None)`, `__len__`, and `size` / `op` / `levels` properties + `stats()`. `op ‚ąą {min, max}`; values must be numbers (bools/non-numerics rejected); `query` needs `0 ‚Č§ lo < hi ‚Č§ n` and `get` needs `0 ‚Č§ i < n` ‚ÄĒ all violations raise `SparseTableError` (non-int indices rejected). `k = (hi‚ąílo).bit_length()‚ąí1` gives `‚Ćälog‚āā‚Ćč` in O(1).
- ‚úÖ 138B: `pradyos/web/sparse_table_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_sparsetable_routes(app, sparse_table=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/sparsetable/build` (body `{values[], op?}`; 422 on missing / bad value / bad op), `GET /api/v1/sparsetable/query` (query `?lo=&hi=`, `Query(ge=0/1)`), `GET /api/v1/sparsetable/get` (query `?i=`), `GET /api/v1/sparsetable/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/sparsetable/reset`.
- ‚úÖ 138C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase138.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `sparse_table` param, and a single `register_sparsetable_routes(app, sparse_table)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 138D: `tests/test_sparse_table.py` (33) + `tests/test_sparsetable_web.py` (21) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against brute force** for every range (both `min` and `max`) across sizes 1‚Ä¶100 + 2 000 queries on a 5 000-element array; edges (single element, full range, adjacent, idempotent overlap, negatives, duplicates, floats); query/get bound checks (raise + `Query(ge=‚Ä¶)` 422s, non-int rejected); build validation (bad value, bad op, non-iterable) + `SparseTableError.detail`; build replaces & op change; reset; `op`/`levels` properties; determinism; 10-thread concurrent read queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `intervaltree`).

**Phase 139 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 295 test modules green. Sovereign KD-Tree (Bentley, 1975) ‚ÄĒ a **k-dimensional spatial index** for nearest-neighbour and orthogonal range search, the platform's first *spatial* structure. Points are stored in a binary tree that **cycles through the dimensions by depth** (axis = depth mod k) and is built by **median split** per axis (so it stays balanced, height `O(log n)`). `nearest(point)` descends toward the query, then **backtracks, pruning any subtree whose splitting plane is farther than the best squared distance found** (that branch cannot hold a closer point ‚ÄĒ comparisons use squared distance, no `sqrt`); `range(lo, hi)` reports all points inside the inclusive axis-aligned box, pruning a child when the box does not cross its splitting plane. This is *different* from the platform's one-dimensional ordered maps and interval tree ‚ÄĒ it answers *multidimensional proximity* queries. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test confirmed `nearest` matched the brute-force minimum distance over 1 600 queries (k = 2 and 3, across many random point sets, compared by distance to allow ties)** and `range` matched a brute-force box scan; `k = 1` and `k = 4`, duplicates, single/empty all check out. Exposed at `/api/v1/kdtree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static ‚ÄĒ built once, median-split per axis). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/kd_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 139A: `pradyos/core/kd_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `KDTreeError(detail)`; `KDTree(points=None, dim=2)` with `build(points)` (static rebuild), `nearest(point)` ‚Üí point|None, `nearest_dist(point)` ‚Üí float|None, `range(lo, hi)` ‚Üí sorted points, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `dim` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. `dim` a positive int; every point/query must have `dim` numeric coordinates; `range` needs `lo[i] ‚Č§ hi[i]` ‚ÄĒ violations raise `KDTreeError`. NN backtracking prunes by `diff¬≤ < best¬≤`; range prunes per axis.
- ‚úÖ 139B: `pradyos/web/kd_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_kdtree_routes(app, kd_tree=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/kdtree/build` (body `{points[], dim?}`; 422 on missing / wrong-dim / non-numeric; may re-create at a new dimension via a shared state holder), `POST /api/v1/kdtree/nearest` (body `{point}` ‚Üí `{nearest, distance}`), `POST /api/v1/kdtree/range` (body `{lo, hi}` ‚Üí `{points, count}`), `GET /api/v1/kdtree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/kdtree/reset`.
- ‚úÖ 139C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase139.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `kd_tree` param, and a single `register_kdtree_routes(app, kd_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 139D: `tests/test_kd_tree.py` (32) + `tests/test_kdtree_web.py` (20) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against brute force** for `nearest` (k=2,3; ~1 600 queries; by distance for ties) and `range` (k=2,3); `nearest_dist`; `k=1` / `k=4`; duplicates / single / empty / negative / float coords; degenerate box; validation (`dim`, wrong-dim, non-numeric, `lo>hi`, non-iterable) + `KDTreeError.detail`; build replaces; reset; balanced-height check; determinism; 10-thread concurrent queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 3-D build & 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `sparsetable`).
- ‚úÖ 139E: `scripts/prove.py` ‚ÄĒ 295 test modules registered (Phase 139 appends `test_kd_tree.py` + `test_kdtree_web.py`).

**Phase 140 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 297 test modules green. Sovereign Radix Tree / Patricia Trie (Morrison, 1968) ‚ÄĒ a **path-compressed prefix tree** for string keys, a new capability for the platform and a distinct, more compact cousin of the plain Trie (P83). Where a trie stores one character per edge, a radix tree **labels each edge with a whole substring** and collapses any chain of single-child nodes, so the node count is bounded by the number of distinguishing prefixes, not total key length ‚ÄĒ the structure behind IP routing tables and autocomplete. `insert` **splits** an edge when a key diverges partway along it; `delete` clears the key and **re-merges** a now-only-child node back into its parent; `prefix_search(prefix)` returns every key under a prefix; `longest_prefix(query)` returns the longest stored key that is a prefix of `query` (the routing-table lookup). This is *different* from P83's character-per-edge trie: edge compression makes it space-efficient and yields `longest_prefix` directly. The reported `compression_ratio` is the honest one ‚ÄĒ **characters stored per node** (a plain trie stores ~1). **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against `dict` matched `search` across a 15 000-op random insert/delete/search mix**, and `prefix_search` / `longest_prefix` matched brute-force scans; the prefix-of-another and delete-then-re-merge edge cases hold, and a shared-prefix set reports `compression_ratio ‚Čą 2.1`. Exposed at `/api/v1/radixtree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/radix_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 140A: `pradyos/core/radix_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `RadixTreeError(detail)`; `RadixTree(seed=0)` with `insert(key, value=None)`, `search(key)`, `contains` / `__contains__`, `delete(key)` ‚Üí bool (with re-merge), `prefix_search(prefix)` ‚Üí sorted `(key, value)` list, `longest_prefix(query)` ‚Üí key|None, `keys()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `seed` properties + `num_nodes()` + `stats()` (`num_keys` / `num_nodes` / `compression_ratio` = chars-per-node). Non-string keys/prefixes (and non-int `seed`) raise `RadixTreeError`.
- ‚úÖ 140B: `pradyos/web/radix_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_radixtree_routes(app, radix_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/radixtree/insert` (body `{key, value?}`; 422 on missing / non-str), `POST /api/v1/radixtree/search` (body `{key}` ‚Üí `{found, value}`), `POST /api/v1/radixtree/prefix_search` (body `{prefix}` ‚Üí `{results, count}`), `DELETE /api/v1/radixtree/delete` (body `{key}` ‚Üí `{deleted, size}`), `GET /api/v1/radixtree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/radixtree/reset` (`longest_prefix` / `contains` stay on the core class).
- ‚úÖ 140C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase140.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `radix_tree` param, and a single `register_radixtree_routes(app, radix_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 140D: `tests/test_radix_tree.py` (35) + `tests/test_radix_tree_web.py` (22) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against `dict`** for insert/search across 2 000 inserts and an 8 000-op insert/delete/search mix; `prefix_search` & `longest_prefix` vs brute force (incl. IP-routing-style); edge split, empty key, prefix-of-another, delete-with-re-merge / re-insert / delete-non-key-internal; `compression_ratio > 1`, `num_nodes`; validation (non-str key/prefix, bad seed) + `RadixTreeError.detail`; reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `kdtree`).

**Phase 141 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 299 test modules green. Sovereign Suffix Array (Manber & Myers, 1990) ‚ÄĒ a **sorted index of all suffixes of a string** that answers substring queries by binary search, a new text-indexing capability that pairs with the Wavelet Tree (P135) and Radix Tree (P140). The array holds the starting positions of every suffix in lexicographic order; because all occurrences of a pattern share a common prefix, they form a **contiguous block** in that order, found by two binary searches (lower/upper bound) ‚ÄĒ so `contains`, `count`, and `positions` are `O(m log n)`. An accompanying **LCP** array records adjacencies, from which the number of **distinct substrings** falls out as `n(n+1)/2 ‚ąí ő£ LCP`. This is *different* from the platform's prefix trees ‚ÄĒ a suffix array indexes *every substring* of one text. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against brute-force scans matched `count`, `positions`, `contains`, the LCP array, and `distinct_substrings` across 37 texts** (incl. `banana`, `mississippi`, repeated chars, random); overlapping matches (`"aa"` in `"aaaa"` ‚Üí 3), full-text and absent patterns, single-char and empty-text edges all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/suffixarray`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static ‚ÄĒ built once from the text). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/suffix_array_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 141A: `pradyos/core/suffix_array.py` ‚ÄĒ `SuffixArrayError(detail)`; `SuffixArray(text="")` with `build(text)` (static rebuild), `contains(pattern)`, `count(pattern)`, `positions(pattern)` (sorted), `suffix_array()`, `lcp_array()`, `distinct_substrings()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `text` properties + `stats()`. Non-string text/pattern and empty patterns raise `SuffixArrayError`; queries are two binary searches over the suffix array.
- ‚úÖ 141B: `pradyos/web/suffix_array_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_suffixarray_routes(app, suffix_array=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/suffixarray/build` (body `{text}`; 422 on missing / non-str), `POST /api/v1/suffixarray/search` (body `{pattern}` ‚Üí `{contains, count, positions}`; 422 on empty/missing), `GET /api/v1/suffixarray/array` (`{suffix_array, lcp_array}`), `GET /api/v1/suffixarray/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/suffixarray/reset`.
- ‚úÖ 141C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase141.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `suffix_array` param, and a single `register_suffixarray_routes(app, suffix_array)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.

**Phase 142 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 301 test modules green. Sovereign Aho-Corasick (Aho & Corasick, 1975) ‚ÄĒ a **multi-pattern string-matching automaton** that finds *all* occurrences of *all* patterns in a text in a single `O(text + matches)` pass, a new capability for the platform. A trie of the patterns is augmented (by a BFS sweep) with **failure links** ‚ÄĒ on a mismatch the link jumps to the longest proper suffix that is still a trie node, so the text is never re-scanned (KMP generalised to a *set* of patterns) ‚ÄĒ and **output sets** that chain every pattern ending at a state via the failure path, so overlapping and nested matches are all reported. `add(pattern)` / `add_many`, `build()` (finalise links; also done lazily on first search), `search(text)` ‚Üí sorted `(pattern, end_index)` matches, plus `count` / `contains_any`. This is *different* from the platform's single-string indexes (Suffix Array/P141, Radix Tree/P140): it matches a *dictionary* against a stream at once. **Verified** (honest): the **failure-link construction was differential-tested against a brute-force multi-find over 300 random pattern-sets**, and the textbook `{he, she, his, hers}` over `"ushers"` yields exactly `[(he,3),(she,3),(hers,5)]`; overlapping (`"aa"`√ó3 in `"aaaa"`), nested, suffix-via-failure-link, dedup, and auto-build-on-search all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/ahocorasick`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/aho_corasick_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 142A: `pradyos/core/aho_corasick.py` ‚ÄĒ `AhoCorasickError(detail)`; `AhoCorasick()` with `add(pattern)` ‚Üí bool (dedup), `add_many(patterns)` ‚Üí count, `build()`, `search(text)` ‚Üí sorted `(pattern, end_index)` list, `count(text)`, `contains_any(text)`, `patterns()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `num_patterns` / `built` properties + `stats()`. Non-string / empty patterns and non-string text raise `AhoCorasickError`; the automaton auto-builds on the first search after a pattern is added (re-adding marks it dirty again).
- ‚úÖ 142B: `pradyos/web/aho_corasick_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_ahocorasick_routes(app, aho_corasick=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/ahocorasick/add` (body `{pattern}`; 422 on missing / empty / non-str), `POST /api/v1/ahocorasick/add_many` (body `{patterns[]}`), `POST /api/v1/ahocorasick/search` (body `{text}` ‚Üí `{matches, count}`), `GET /api/v1/ahocorasick/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/ahocorasick/reset`.

Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 142D: `tests/test_aho_corasick.py` (33) + `tests/test_aho_corasick_web.py` (20) ‚ÄĒ the classic `ushers` example, nested & substring-of-another patterns, unicode; **a differential test against brute force over 300 random pattern-sets**; overlapping count, `contains_any`, single-char patterns, suffix-match-via-failure-link; edges (no patterns, empty text, absent, pattern-longer); dedup + add/dup return values; auto-build / re-add-marks-dirty / explicit build; `add_many`; validation (non-str / empty pattern, non-str text, non-iterable) + `AhoCorasickError.detail`; reset; `patterns()` sorted; determinism; 10-thread concurrent search; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `suffixarray`).

**Phase 143 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 303 test modules green. Sovereign Binary (XOR) Trie ‚ÄĒ a **bitwise trie over fixed-width integers** that answers **maximum-XOR** queries greedily, a new capability for the platform. Each integer is stored as a root-to-leaf path of its bits from the most significant down (`width` levels, default 32); `max_xor(q)` walks the trie preferring, at every level, the child whose bit is *opposite* to `q`'s (maximising that XOR bit), so a single `O(width)` descent finds `max(q ^ x)` over all stored `x`. With per-node counts (a multiset) it also supports `min_xor`, `count_xor_less(q, k)` (stored values whose XOR with `q` is `< k` ‚ÄĒ the building block of XOR range queries), `insert`, `remove` (pruning emptied subtrees), and `contains`. This is *different* in mechanism from the character trie (P83) and radix tree (P140): a fixed-depth *binary* trie keyed on bit position ‚ÄĒ the structure behind max-XOR-pair and XOR-range problems. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test matched `max_xor` / `min_xor` / `count_xor_less` / `contains` against brute force over 1 800 queries (widths 4‚Äď32)** and an 8 000-op insert/remove multiset against a `Counter`; the classic max-XOR-pair (`max over x of max_xor(x)`) equals the brute-force best pair. Exposed at `/api/v1/xortrie`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/xor_trie_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 143A: `pradyos/core/xor_trie.py` ‚ÄĒ `XorTrieError(detail)`; `XorTrie(width=32)` with `insert(value)`, `remove(value)` ‚Üí bool, `contains` / `__contains__`, `max_xor(query)` / `min_xor(query)` (raise on empty), `count_xor_less(query, k)`, `reset(width=None)`, `__len__`, and `size` / `width` properties + `stats()`. `width ‚ąą [1, 256]`; values/queries must be ints in `[0, 2^width)`; non-int `k` rejected ‚ÄĒ all raise `XorTrieError` (bools rejected). Per-node counts make it a multiset.
- ‚úÖ 143B: `pradyos/web/xor_trie_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_xortrie_routes(app, xor_trie=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/xortrie/insert` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / out-of-range), `DELETE /api/v1/xortrie/remove` (body `{value}` ‚Üí `{removed, size}`), `POST /api/v1/xortrie/query` (body `{query}` ‚Üí `{max_xor, min_xor}`; 422 on empty trie), `POST /api/v1/xortrie/count_xor_less` (body `{query, k}`), `GET /api/v1/xortrie/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/xortrie/reset` (`contains` stays on the core class).
- ‚úÖ 143C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase143.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `xor_trie` param, and a single `register_xortrie_routes(app, xor_trie)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 143D: `tests/test_xor_trie.py` (33) + `tests/test_xor_trie_web.py` (22) ‚ÄĒ **differential vs brute force** for `max_xor`/`min_xor`/`count_xor_less`/`contains` across widths 4‚Äď32, an 8 000-op insert/remove multiset, and the **classic max-XOR-pair**; counted duplicates, `k` bounds, single value, empty raises; validation (`width`, out-of-range / negative / bool value, out-of-range query, non-int `k`) + `XorTrieError.detail`; reset / reconfigure width; `num_nodes`; determinism; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `ahocorasick`).

**Phase 144 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 305 test modules green. Sovereign Min-Max Heap (Atkinson, Sack, Santoro & Strothotte, 1986) ‚ÄĒ a **double-ended priority queue** giving `O(1)` access to *both* the minimum and the maximum and `O(log n)` `extract_min` / `extract_max`, a new capability for the platform (the Skew Heap of P136 is a min-only meldable queue). It is a single array-backed binary heap whose levels **alternate**: a node on an even (min) level is `‚Č§` all its descendants; on an odd (max) level it is `‚Č•` all theirs. Insertion bubbles up against *grandparents* on the matching level type; `extract_min` / `extract_max` sift down by repeatedly swapping with the smallest/largest among a node's children *and grandchildren* (with a parent fix-up when a grandchild is chosen) ‚ÄĒ the level-parity logic that makes both ends cheap at once. Supports `push` / `push_many`, `peek_min` / `peek_max`, `extract_min` / `extract_max`, `keys_sorted`, `__len__`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test confirmed `extract_min` yields ascending and `extract_max` descending order over 150 trials, an interleaved `extract_min`/`extract_max` mix matched a sorted deque over 100 trials, and the min-max invariant held through every push and extract**; level-boundary sizes 1‚Äď5, a 2 000-element drain, duplicates and strings all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/minmaxheap`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; sift-down iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/min_max_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 144A: `pradyos/core/min_max_heap.py` ‚ÄĒ `MinMaxHeapError(detail)`; `MinMaxHeap()` with `push(value)` / `push_many(values)` ‚Üí count, `peek_min()` / `peek_max()` (raise on empty), `extract_min()` / `extract_max()` (raise on empty), `keys_sorted()`, `is_empty()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `kind` properties + `stats()`. Values must be one orderable kind (`int`/`float` or `str`); bools, non-orderable values and mixed kinds raise `MinMaxHeapError`. Level parity is `(i+1).bit_length()‚ąí1 mod 2`; bubble-up compares grandparents; sift-down scans children+grandchildren.
- ‚úÖ 144B: `pradyos/web/min_max_heap_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_minmaxheap_routes(app, min_max_heap=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/minmaxheap/push` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / bad / mixed-kind), `POST /api/v1/minmaxheap/extract_min` (422 on empty), `POST /api/v1/minmaxheap/extract_max` (422 on empty), `GET /api/v1/minmaxheap/peek` (`min`/`max` null when empty), `GET /api/v1/minmaxheap/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/minmaxheap/reset`.
- ‚úÖ 144C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase144.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `min_max_heap` param, and a single `register_minmaxheap_routes(app, min_max_heap)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 144D: `tests/test_min_max_heap.py` (32) + `tests/test_min_max_heap_web.py` (20) ‚ÄĒ **differential vs sorted** for ascending/descending drains and **interleaved extract vs a sorted deque**, plus the **min-max invariant** through pushes and extracts; level-boundary sizes, 2 000-drain, duplicates, floats/negatives, strings; empty-op & validation raises (bool, non-orderable, mixed kind, non-iterable) + `MinMaxHeapError.detail`; `push_many`; `kind` resets when emptied; reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent pushes; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `xortrie`).

**Phase 145 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 307 test modules green. Sovereign Cartesian Tree (Vuillemin, 1980) ‚ÄĒ a **binary tree built from a sequence** that is simultaneously a **binary-search tree on position** and a **min-heap on value**, a new capability for the platform. It is constructed in `O(n)` by a single left-to-right scan with a stack (each new element pops larger-valued nodes off the right spine, adopts the last popped as its left child, becomes the right child of whatever remains), and its in-order traversal recovers the original index order. Its defining property is the **range-minimum ‚ÜĒ lowest-common-ancestor equivalence**: the minimum of any index range `[l, r]` is the value at the LCA of positions `l` and `r` (here via parent pointers + a depth array) ‚ÄĒ so `range_min` is an LCA lookup, with leftmost-on-ties. Supports `build`, `range_min(l, r)` / `range_argmin`, `inorder`, `sequence`, and exposes the `structure` (parent/left/right arrays). This is *different* from the doubling-table Sparse Table (P138): the same range-min query, via an explicit tree that also underlies treap construction and suffix-tree links. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test confirmed `inorder == 0‚Ä¶n-1`, the BST+min-heap invariants, and `range_min` against a brute scan over *every* range across 120+ random sequences**; the root is the global argmin, ties take the leftmost, and a degenerate sorted 5 000-element input builds and queries with no recursion error. Exposed at `/api/v1/cartesiantree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/cartesian_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 145A: `pradyos/core/cartesian_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `CartesianTreeError(detail)`; `CartesianTree(values=None)` with `build(values)` (static rebuild), `range_min(lo, hi)` / `range_argmin(lo, hi)`, `inorder()`, `sequence()`, `structure()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `root_index` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. Values must be numbers (bools/non-numerics rejected); `range_min` needs `0 ‚Č§ lo ‚Č§ hi < n` (non-int rejected) ‚ÄĒ all raise `CartesianTreeError`. Build is a stack; LCA is a parent-walk over a precomputed depth array.
- ‚úÖ 145B: `pradyos/web/cartesian_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_cartesiantree_routes(app, cartesian_tree=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/cartesiantree/build` (body `{values[]}`; 422 on missing / non-numeric), `GET /api/v1/cartesiantree/range_min` (query `?lo=&hi=`, `Query(ge=0)` ‚Üí `{min, argmin}`), `GET /api/v1/cartesiantree/structure`, `GET /api/v1/cartesiantree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/cartesiantree/reset`.
- ‚úÖ 145C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase145.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `cartesian_tree` param, and a single `register_cartesiantree_routes(app, cartesian_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 145D: `tests/test_cartesian_tree.py` (33) + `tests/test_cartesian_tree_web.py` (17) ‚ÄĒ **differential vs brute** for `inorder`, BST+min-heap invariants, and `range_min`/`range_argmin` over every range across 120+ sequences; degenerate ascending/descending 5 000 (no recursion); leftmost-on-ties, root-is-global-argmin, single/empty, floats/negatives; validation (non-numeric, bool, `lo>hi`, out-of-range, non-int) + `CartesianTreeError.detail`; build replaces; reset; `structure`/`sequence`/height; determinism; 10-thread concurrent queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `minmaxheap`).

**Phase 146 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 309 test modules green. Sovereign 2D Fenwick Tree (2D Binary Indexed Tree; Fenwick, 1994) ‚ÄĒ a **2-D point-update / rectangle-sum index** in `O(log¬≤n)` per operation, a new capability for the platform (the Fenwick Tree of P80 is one-dimensional). Over an `R √ó C` grid each internal `(i, j)` holds the sum of a rectangle of cells fixed by the low-bits of `i` and `j`; `update(i, j, delta)` walks `i += i&-i`, `j += j&-j` and a prefix sum walks them down ‚ÄĒ so the sum of any sub-rectangle is **four prefix sums** by inclusion-exclusion. Supports `update`, `point_value`, `prefix_sum(i, j)` (sum of `[0..i] √ó [0..j]`), `range_sum(r1, c1, r2, c2)`, and `total`. This is *different* from the 1-D Fenwick (P80) and the range-*min* structures (Sparse Table/P138, Cartesian Tree/P145): it answers 2-D rectangle *sum* queries under point updates. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute reference grid matched `prefix_sum`, `range_sum`, and `point_value` over 480 queries across six grid shapes** plus a 50√ó50 grid with 3 000 updates; negatives/accumulation, full-grid, single row/column and 1√ó1 edges all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/fenwick2d`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/fenwick2d_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 146A: `pradyos/core/fenwick_2d.py` ‚ÄĒ `Fenwick2DError(detail)`; `Fenwick2D(rows=16, cols=16)` with `update(i, j, delta)`, `prefix_sum(i, j)`, `range_sum(r1, c1, r2, c2)`, `point_value(i, j)`, `total()`, `reset(rows=None, cols=None)`, and `rows` / `cols` properties + `stats()`. `rows`/`cols` positive ints; coordinates ints in range; `delta` a number; `range_sum` needs `r1 ‚Č§ r2`, `c1 ‚Č§ c2` ‚ÄĒ all violations raise `Fenwick2DError` (bools rejected). Updates and prefix sums are nested low-bit walks; `range_sum` is inclusion-exclusion of four prefix sums.
- ‚úÖ 146B: `pradyos/web/fenwick2d_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_fenwick2d_routes(app, fenwick2d=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/fenwick2d/update` (body `{i, j, delta}`; 422 on missing / out-of-range / bad delta), `GET /api/v1/fenwick2d/prefix_sum` (query `?i=&j=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `GET /api/v1/fenwick2d/range_sum` (query `?r1=&c1=&r2=&c2=`), `GET /api/v1/fenwick2d/point_value` (query `?i=&j=`), `GET /api/v1/fenwick2d/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/fenwick2d/reset` (body `{rows?, cols?}`).
- ‚úÖ 146C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase146.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `fenwick2d` param, and a single `register_fenwick2d_routes(app, fenwick2d)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 146D: `tests/test_fenwick_2d.py` (31) + `tests/test_fenwick2d_web.py` (23) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against a brute grid** for `prefix_sum`/`range_sum`/`point_value` across six shapes + a 50√ó50/3 000-update grid; 1√ó1, accumulation/negatives, full-grid, single row/column, corners; validation (out-of-range, `r1>r2`, non-int coords, non-num delta, bad dims, bool) + `Fenwick2DError.detail`; reset / reconfigure; determinism; 10-thread concurrent updates; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `cartesiantree`).

**Phase 147 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 311 test modules green. Sovereign Sqrt Decomposition ‚ÄĒ a **block-decomposition range structure** supporting `O(‚ąön)` **range-add** and **range-sum** over an array, a new *technique* for the platform (distinct from Segment Tree/P81's `O(log n)` and the point-update Fenwick/P80). The array is split into `‚Čą‚ąön` contiguous blocks, each carrying a block sum and a **lazy "add" tag** applied conceptually to every element of the block but not yet pushed down; the true value of element `i` is `a[i] + tag[block(i)]`. A range update touches the `O(‚ąön)` fully-covered blocks via their tags (`tag[b] += delta`) and the two partial boundary blocks element-wise (updating both the element and its block sum); a range query sums each covered block's `block_sum + tag¬∑block_len` plus the partial ends ‚ÄĒ both `O(‚ąön)`. Supports `range_add(lo, hi, delta)`, `range_sum(lo, hi)`, `point_query(i)`, absolute point `update(i, value)`, `build`, `total`, and `reset`. This is *different* from the platform's other range structures: a deliberately simple `O(‚ąön)` block method with lazy tags ‚ÄĒ the classic stepping-stone to segment-tree lazy propagation. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute reference array matched `range_sum` and `point_query` over 349 random queries across nine array sizes** plus a 1 000-element / 500-update differential; exact-block / spanning / within-one-block / whole-array ranges, update interacting with an active tag, negative deltas, 1-element and float arrays all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/sqrtdecomp`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/sqrt_decomposition_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 147A: `pradyos/core/sqrt_decomposition.py` ‚ÄĒ `SqrtDecompositionError(detail)`; `SqrtDecomposition(values=None)` with `range_add(lo, hi, delta)`, `range_sum(lo, hi)`, `point_query(i)`, `update(i, value)`, `total()`, `build(values)`, `reset()`, `len()` / `size` / `block_size` / `num_blocks` + `stats()`. `values` numbers; indices ints in range; `lo ‚Č§ hi`; `delta` / `value` numbers ‚ÄĒ all violations raise `SqrtDecompositionError` (bools rejected). `block_size = ‚Ćä‚ąön‚Ćč`; covered blocks updated via a lazy tag, partial boundary blocks element-wise; every operation iterative.
- ‚úÖ 147B: `pradyos/web/sqrt_decomposition_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_sqrtdecomp_routes(app, sqrt_decomposition=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/sqrtdecomp/range_add` (body `{lo, hi, delta}`; 422 on missing / out-of-range / `lo>hi` / bad delta), `GET /api/v1/sqrtdecomp/range_sum` (query `?lo=&hi=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `GET /api/v1/sqrtdecomp/point_query` (query `?i=`), `POST /api/v1/sqrtdecomp/update` (body `{i, value}`), `GET /api/v1/sqrtdecomp/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/sqrtdecomp/reset` (body `{values?}` ‚ÄĒ rebuild from array / clear).

**Phase 148 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 313 test modules green. Sovereign Li Chao Tree ‚ÄĒ a **line container** over a fixed integer x-domain `[x_min, x_max]` that maintains a set of lines `y = m¬∑x + b` and answers the **minimum (or maximum) `y` at any query `x`** in `O(log C)` (`C = x_max ‚ąí x_min + 1`), the segment-tree "Li Chao" form of the convex-hull-trick / kinetic line container ‚ÄĒ the platform's *first* line-container structure. It is an implicit segment tree over the x-range; each node owns the line dominant at its segment midpoint, and `add_line` keeps the midpoint-winner at the node while pushing the loser into the *one* half-segment where it can still become dominant, and `query(x)` takes the best value among the lines on the root‚Üíleaf path for `x`. Max-mode is served by the same min machinery via sign-flipped lines. This is *different* from every range-sum/range-min index (Fenwick/P80, Segment Tree/P81, Sparse Table/P138, Cartesian Tree/P145, 2D Fenwick/P146, Sqrt Decomposition/P147) and the spatial KD-Tree/P139: it answers linear-function extrema, not array aggregates. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute list of lines matched min-mode over 2 910 queries and max-mode over 2 400 queries** across 80 random line sets, and **every one of the 120 insertion-order permutations of a 5-line set produced identical query results** (the "push loser to the winnable half" logic is order-invariant); float lines, parallel/crossing lines, domain edges, single-point domain and the empty‚Üí`None` case all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/lichao`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; add/query descents iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/li_chao_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 148A: `pradyos/core/li_chao_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `LiChaoTreeError(detail)`; `LiChaoTree(x_min=0, x_max=1_000_000, mode='min')` with `add_line(m, b)`, `query(x)`, `reset(x_min=None, x_max=None, mode=None)`, `len()` / `num_lines` / `x_min` / `x_max` / `mode` + `stats()`. `x_min ‚Č§ x_max` ints; `mode ‚ąą {min, max}`; `m`/`b` numbers; `x` an int in domain ‚ÄĒ all violations raise `LiChaoTreeError` (bools rejected). `query` returns `None` when no lines added. Implicit segment tree keyed by `(l, r)` in a dict; add/query iterative; max-mode via sign-flipped lines.
- ‚úÖ 148B: `pradyos/web/li_chao_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_lichao_routes(app, li_chao_tree=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/lichao/add_line` (body `{m, b}`; 422 missing / non-num), `POST /api/v1/lichao/add_lines` (body `{lines: [[m, b], ‚Ä¶]}`; 422 bad shape / non-num), `GET /api/v1/lichao/query` (query `?x=`, negatives allowed; `value` may be null), `GET /api/v1/lichao/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/lichao/reset` (body `{x_min?, x_max?, mode?}`).
- ‚úÖ 148C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase148.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `li_chao_tree` param, and a single `register_lichao_routes(app, li_chao_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 148D: `tests/test_li_chao_tree.py` (35) + `tests/test_li_chao_tree_web.py` (20) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against a brute line list** for min (2 910 queries) and max (2 400 queries) modes + a 120-permutation order-invariance check; float lines, 50-line sets, a 0‚Ä¶10‚ĀĻ domain, negative domains, parallel/crossing lines, domain edges, single-point domain, empty‚Üí`None`; validation (`x_min>x_max`, bad mode, non-num line, out-of-domain / non-int `x`, bool) + `LiChaoTreeError.detail`; reset / reconfigure; determinism; 4-thread concurrent `add_line`s; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `sqrtdecomp`).

**Phase 149 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 315 test modules green. Sovereign Persistent Segment Tree ‚ÄĒ a **fully-persistent (versioned) range-sum index**: the array starts as *version 0*, and every point `update` returns a *new version* in `O(log n)` via **path-copying** (the `O(log n)` nodes on the root‚Üíleaf path are copied while every untouched subtree is *shared* with the previous version), so any past version stays queryable forever in `O(log n)` and `k` updates cost only `O(k log n)` extra nodes. This is the platform's **first persistent / immutable data structure** ‚ÄĒ distinct from every *ephemeral* range index (Fenwick/P80, Segment Tree/P81, Sparse Table/P138, 2D Fenwick/P146, Sqrt Decomposition/P147) and from the Li Chao line-container/P148: those keep one mutable state, this keeps the entire history. Nodes live in append-only parallel arrays (`_sum`/`_left`/`_right`) indexed by node-id and are never mutated after creation ‚ÄĒ which is exactly what makes old versions safe. Supports `build(values)` ‚Üí version 0, `update(version, i, value)` ‚Üí a new version index, `range_sum(version, lo, hi)`, `point_query(version, i)`, and `num_versions`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a list of per-version reference arrays matched `range_sum` and `point_query` over 1 275 queries on *every* version (including the oldest) after many updates** across nine sizes ‚ÄĒ proving immutability / no aliasing ‚ÄĒ plus a 200-element / 300-update differential, branching history (updating an old version twice), a 20-deep update chain, single-element / power-of-two / non-power-of-two shapes, floats and negatives. Exposed at `/api/v1/perseg`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; build / update / query all iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/persistent_segment_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 149A: `pradyos/core/persistent_segment_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `PersistentSegmentTreeError(detail)`; `PersistentSegmentTree(values=None)` with `build(values)`, `update(version, i, value)` ‚Üí new version index, `range_sum(version, lo, hi)`, `point_query(version, i)`, `reset()`, `size` / `num_versions` / `len()` + `stats()`. `values` non-empty numbers; `version` in range; indices ints in `[0, n)`; `lo ‚Č§ hi`; `value` a number ‚ÄĒ all violations raise `PersistentSegmentTreeError` (bools rejected). Append-only node arrays; iterative post-order build, iterative path-copy update, iterative query.
- ‚úÖ 149B: `pradyos/web/persistent_segment_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_perseg_routes(app, persistent_segment_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/perseg/build` (body `{values}`; 422 missing / empty / non-num), `POST /api/v1/perseg/update` (body `{version, i, value}`), `GET /api/v1/perseg/range_sum` (query `?version=&lo=&hi=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `GET /api/v1/perseg/point_query` (query `?version=&i=`), `GET /api/v1/perseg/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/perseg/reset`.

Existing routes untouched.

**Phase 150 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 317 test modules green. Sovereign Pairing Heap (Fredman‚ÄďSedgewick‚ÄďSleator‚ÄďTarjan, 1986) ‚ÄĒ a self-adjusting **mergeable min-priority-queue** whose distinguishing feature is **`decrease_key` in `O(log n)` amortized** (with `O(1)` `insert` / `find_min` / internal `meld`), a capability the platform's other heaps lack (the Skew Heap/P136 melds but exposes no key-decrease; the Min-Max Heap/P144 is double-ended but neither melds nor decreases keys). It is a single multiway tree kept min-at-root: `insert` melds in a one-node tree, `delete_min` removes the root and re-pairs its children with the classic **two-pass** merge (left‚Üíright meld consecutive pairs, then right‚Üíleft accumulate), and `decrease_key` lowers a node's value, detaches its subtree, and melds it back at the root. Nodes live in append-only parallel arrays (`_val`/`_child`/`_sibling`/`_parent`) indexed by a **stable integer handle** returned from `insert`, which is what makes `decrease_key` addressable. Supports `insert(value)` ‚Üí handle, `find_min`, `find_min_handle`, `delete_min`, `decrease_key(handle, value)`, `size`, `is_empty`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute `{handle ‚Üí value}` dict matched `find_min` after every op over 4 800 random insert/delete_min/decrease_key operations**, and a **full-drain == `sorted` check across 60 random trials** plus a 3 000-element drain; decrease-to-new-min, decrease-the-root, decrease-to-same-value, duplicates, insertion-order independence, and dead/bad-handle rejection all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/pairingheap`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; iterative (two-pass delete-min, `O(1)` meld/detach). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/pairing_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 150A: `pradyos/core/pairing_heap.py` ‚ÄĒ `PairingHeapError(detail)`; `PairingHeap()` with `insert(value)` ‚Üí handle, `find_min`, `find_min_handle`, `delete_min`, `decrease_key(handle, value)`, `is_empty`, `reset`, `size` / `len()` + `stats()`. `value` a number; `handle` a live int handle; `decrease_key` must not increase the value ‚ÄĒ all violations raise `PairingHeapError` (bools rejected; empty `find_min`/`delete_min` raise). Append-only `_val`/`_child`/`_sibling`/`_parent` arrays; `O(1)` meld, iterative two-pass `delete_min`, sibling-walk `decrease_key` detach.
- ‚úÖ 150B: `pradyos/web/pairing_heap_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_pairingheap_routes(app, pairing_heap=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/pairingheap/insert` (body `{value}`; 422 missing / non-num), `GET /api/v1/pairingheap/find_min` (`min` null when empty), `POST /api/v1/pairingheap/delete_min` (422 if empty), `POST /api/v1/pairingheap/decrease_key` (body `{handle, value}`; 422 bad/dead handle / key-increase), `GET /api/v1/pairingheap/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/pairingheap/reset`.
- ‚úÖ 150C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase150.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `pairing_heap` param, and a single `register_pairingheap_routes(app, pairing_heap)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 150D: `tests/test_pairing_heap.py` (37) + `tests/test_pairing_heap_web.py` (17) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against a brute `{handle‚Üívalue}` dict** (4 800 mixed ops) + full-drain == `sorted` (60 trials) + 3 000-element drain; decrease-to-new-min / decrease-root / decrease-same, duplicates, insertion-order independence, negatives, floats; validation (empty pop, non-num, bad/dead/non-int handle, key-increase, bool) + `PairingHeapError.detail`; reset; determinism; 4-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s and a decrease_key‚Üídrain workflow + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `perseg`).
- ‚úÖ 150E: `scripts/prove.py` ‚ÄĒ 317 test modules registered (Phase 150 appends `test_pairing_heap.py` + `test_pairing_heap_web.py`).

**Phase 151 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 319 test modules green. Sovereign Suffix Automaton (Blumer et al. 1985 / Crochemore) ‚ÄĒ the **minimal deterministic automaton recognizing every substring** of a string, built **online** in `O(n)` amortized by appending characters and splitting/cloning states along suffix links. Paths from the initial state spell exactly the substrings, so `contains` is an `O(|p|)` walk, and the **number of distinct substrings** is `ő£ (len[v] ‚ąí len[link[v]])` over every non-initial state. This is the platform's first automaton-of-all-substrings ‚ÄĒ distinct from the sorted-suffix index (Suffix Array/P141, which binary-searches sorted suffixes) and the multi-pattern failure-link trie (Aho‚ÄďCorasick/P142, which scans for a fixed dictionary). States live in parallel `len`/`link`/`trans` lists (transitions are per-state dicts, so the alphabet may be ASCII or Unicode). Supports `extend(ch)` / `build(text)`, `contains(pattern)`, `distinct_substrings()`, `num_states`, `length`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against the brute set of all substrings matched `distinct_substrings()` exactly across 300 random strings** (alphabets of 3 and 8, up to 60 chars) plus a 2 000-character string, and **`contains` matched brute membership over 1 500 queries** (substrings and non-substrings); `aaaa`‚Üí4, `abab`/`abcabc`/`banana`, single-char, empty, Unicode (`h√©llo‚ėÉh√©llo`), `num_states ‚Č§ 2n`, and `extend`-incremental == `build` all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/suffixautomaton`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; iterative online construction (no recursion). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/suffix_automaton_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 151A: `pradyos/core/suffix_automaton.py` ‚ÄĒ `SuffixAutomatonError(detail)`; `SuffixAutomaton(text=None)` with `extend(ch)`, `build(text)`, `contains(pattern)`, `distinct_substrings()`, `reset()`, `num_states` / `length` / `len()` + `stats()`. `extend` takes a single-character string; `build`/`contains` take strings ‚ÄĒ all violations raise `SuffixAutomatonError`. Parallel `_len`/`_link`/`_trans` lists; online suffix-link walk with state cloning, all `while`-loop iterative.
- ‚úÖ 151B: `pradyos/web/suffix_automaton_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_suffixautomaton_routes(app, suffix_automaton=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/suffixautomaton/build` (body `{text}`; 422 missing / non-str), `POST /api/v1/suffixautomaton/extend` (body `{ch}`; 422 non-single-char), `GET /api/v1/suffixautomaton/contains` (query `?pattern=`, empty ‚Üí true), `GET /api/v1/suffixautomaton/distinct_substrings`, `GET /api/v1/suffixautomaton/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/suffixautomaton/reset`.
- ‚úÖ 151C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase151.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `suffix_automaton` param, and a single `register_suffixautomaton_routes(app, suffix_automaton)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 151D: `tests/test_suffix_automaton.py` (35) + `tests/test_suffix_automaton_web.py` (18) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against the brute substring set** for `distinct_substrings` (300 strings + a 2 000-char string) and `contains` (1 500 queries); structured strings, Unicode, `num_states ‚Č§ 2n`, extend==build, every-substring-contained; validation (non-str build, multi-char/non-str extend, non-str contains) + `SuffixAutomatonError.detail`; build / reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent `contains` + all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `pairingheap`).
- ‚úÖ 151E: `scripts/prove.py` ‚ÄĒ 319 test modules registered (Phase 151 appends `test_suffix_automaton.py` + `test_suffix_automaton_web.py`).

**Phase 152 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 321 test modules green. Sovereign van Emde Boas Tree (van Emde Boas, 1975) ‚ÄĒ a **bounded-integer ordered set over a universe `[0, U)`** (`U` rounded up to a power of two) supporting `insert` / `delete` / `member` / `minimum` / `maximum` and, most distinctively, **`successor` / `predecessor` in `O(log log U)`** ‚ÄĒ a complexity class no existing platform structure offers, and the platform's first integer-universe (van-Emde-Boas-recursion) structure, distinct from comparison-ordered sets and from every hash/sketch. Each node recurses into a `‚ąöU` *summary* plus up to `‚ąöU` *clusters*, storing the running `min` **lazily** (the minimum is held outside its cluster) so every operation makes only one deep recursive call ‚ÄĒ the `T(u) = T(‚ąöu) + O(1)` recurrence. The recursion is carried by an internal lock-free node; the public class holds a single lock at the top so descent never re-enters it, and clusters/summaries are created lazily for `O(n)` memory. Supports `insert(x)` ‚Üí added?, `delete(x)` ‚Üí present?, `member(x)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `successor(x)`, `predecessor(x)`, `size`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a sorted-set ground truth matched `member` / `minimum` / `maximum` / `successor` / `predecessor` after every op over 20 960 query points across six universes**, an **exhaustive successor/predecessor sweep over all of `[0, 256)`**, and an **8 000-operation differential on `U = 65 536`**; duplicate-insert / delete-absent no-ops, single-element and boundary (`0`, `U‚ąí1`) behaviour, universe rounding (`1000 ‚Üí 1024`), full-universe successor walk and delete-min drain all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/veb`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; recursion depth is structurally bounded at `O(log log U) ‚Č§ ~5` (never input-dependent). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/van_emde_boas_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 152A: `pradyos/core/van_emde_boas.py` ‚ÄĒ `VanEmdeBoasError(detail)`; `VanEmdeBoas(universe=65536)` with `insert(x)` ‚Üí bool, `delete(x)` ‚Üí bool, `member(x)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `successor(x)`, `predecessor(x)`, `reset()`, `is_empty()`, `size` / `len()` / `universe` + `stats()`. `universe` a positive int (rounded up to a power of two); `x` an int in `[0, universe)` ‚ÄĒ all violations raise `VanEmdeBoasError` (bools rejected). Internal lock-free `_VEBNode` recursion with lazy min and lazily-created summary/clusters; public methods take the lock once.
- ‚úÖ 152B: `pradyos/web/van_emde_boas_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_veb_routes(app, van_emde_boas=None)` mounts 7 routes: `POST /api/v1/veb/insert` (body `{value}`), `POST /api/v1/veb/delete` (body `{value}`), `GET /api/v1/veb/member` (query `?value=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `GET /api/v1/veb/successor` (may be null), `GET /api/v1/veb/predecessor` (may be null), `GET /api/v1/veb/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/veb/reset`. Out-of-range / non-int ‚Üí 422.
- ‚úÖ 152C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase152.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `van_emde_boas` param, and a single `register_veb_routes(app, van_emde_boas)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.

**Phase 153 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 323 test modules green. Sovereign PR Quadtree (point-region quadtree; Finkel & Bentley, 1974) ‚ÄĒ a **2-D spatial index over a fixed rectangle** storing *named* points, recursively subdividing a cell into four equal quadrants whenever a leaf would exceed one point (down to `max_depth`). It answers exact lookup, **axis-aligned rectangle range queries**, and **nearest-neighbour** (Euclidean, branch-and-bound over a min-heap of node lower-bounds), with dynamic insert/delete and cell collapse on delete ‚ÄĒ the platform's first space-subdivision-by-quadrant structure, distinct from the median-split KD-Tree/P139 (a static nearest-neighbour index over the points): the quadtree subdivides *space*. A side `id ‚Üí (x, y)` index gives O(1) delete/move. Subdivision depth is bounded by `max_depth` (never input-dependent), so descent is a bounded loop and range/nearest queries use an explicit stack / min-heap (no recursion). Supports `insert(point_id, x, y)` (move on duplicate id), `delete(point_id)`, `search(x, y)`, `range_query(x_min, y_min, x_max, y_max)`, `nearest(x, y)`, `num_points`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): **`range_query` matched a brute point set across 30+ random sub-rectangles of a 100√ó100 grid**, **`nearest` matched brute min-Euclidean over 150 queries** (1 000- and 500-point clouds, incl. after deletes), full-bounds returns all 1 000 inserted, delete-all collapses the tree to a single root node, move-on-duplicate-id, coincident-point buckets at `max_depth`, and determinism (same seed ‚Üí identical tree) all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/prquadtree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/pr_quadtree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 153A: `pradyos/core/pr_quadtree.py` ‚ÄĒ `PRQuadtreeError(detail)`; `PRQuadtree(x_min, y_min, x_max, y_max, max_depth=12)` with `insert(point_id, x, y)`, `delete(point_id)` ‚Üí bool, `search(x, y)`, `range_query(...)` ‚Üí sorted ids, `nearest(x, y)`, `reset()`, `num_points` / `len()` + `stats()`. Bounds must satisfy `x_min<x_max`, `y_min<y_max`; `max_depth ‚Č• 1`; points must be numeric and in-bounds; `point_id` hashable / non-None ‚ÄĒ violations raise `PRQuadtreeError`. Bounded-depth descent; explicit-stack range query; min-heap branch-and-bound nearest; collapse-on-delete.
- ‚úÖ 153B: `pradyos/web/pr_quadtree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_pr_quadtree_routes(app, pr_quadtree=None)` mounts 7 routes: `POST /api/v1/prquadtree/insert` (body `{point_id, x, y}`), `POST /api/v1/prquadtree/delete` (body `{point_id}`), `GET /api/v1/prquadtree/search` (`?x=&y=`), `GET /api/v1/prquadtree/range_query` (`?x_min=&y_min=&x_max=&y_max=`), `GET /api/v1/prquadtree/nearest` (`?x=&y=`, may be null), `GET /api/v1/prquadtree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/prquadtree/reset`. Out-of-bounds / non-num / inverted-rect ‚Üí 422.

**Phase 154 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 325 test modules green. Sovereign Fibonacci Heap (Fredman & Tarjan, 1984) ‚ÄĒ a **mergeable min-priority-queue with `O(1)` amortized `insert` / `find_min` / `decrease_key` and `O(log n)` amortized `extract_min`**, the asymptotically optimal heap behind Dijkstra/Prim. It is a forest of heap-ordered trees with a min-pointer; `extract_min` **consolidates** roots of equal degree (linking the larger-key root under the smaller via a degree array until all root degrees are distinct), and `decrease_key` **cuts** a node to the root list with **cascading cuts** up through already-marked ancestors ‚ÄĒ a different mechanism from the two-pass Pairing Heap/P150 (and unlike the meld-only Skew Heap/P136 or the double-ended Min-Max Heap/P144). Nodes are objects in circular doubly-linked sibling lists; a stable integer handle from `insert` (mapped to its node) makes `decrease_key` addressable. Supports `insert(value)` ‚Üí handle, `find_min`, `find_min_handle`, `extract_min`, `decrease_key(handle, value)`, `size`, `is_empty`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **full-drain == `sorted` check across 60 random trials** plus a 5 000-element drain, a **differential test against a brute `{handle ‚Üí value}` dict matched `find_min` after every op over 10 000 random insert/extract_min/decrease_key operations**, and a **dedicated cascading-cut stress** (extract to force consolidation into deep trees, then 80 `decrease_key`s) ‚ÄĒ find_min and the final drain both correct; decrease-to-new-min, duplicates, floats/negatives, insertion-order independence, and dead/bad-handle rejection all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/fibonacci`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; iterative consolidate + cascading cut (no recursion). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/fibonacci_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 154A: `pradyos/core/fibonacci_heap.py` ‚ÄĒ `FibonacciHeapError(detail)`; `FibonacciHeap()` with `insert(value)` ‚Üí handle, `find_min`, `find_min_handle`, `extract_min`, `decrease_key(handle, value)`, `is_empty`, `reset`, `size` / `len()` + `stats()`. `value` a number; `handle` a live int handle; `decrease_key` must not increase the value ‚ÄĒ all violations raise `FibonacciHeapError` (bools rejected; empty `find_min`/`extract_min` raise). Circular doubly-linked root/child lists; iterative degree-array consolidate and iterative cascading cut.
- ‚úÖ 154B: `pradyos/web/fibonacci_heap_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_fibonacci_routes(app, fibonacci_heap=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/fibonacci/insert` (body `{value}`), `GET /api/v1/fibonacci/find_min` (`min` null when empty), `POST /api/v1/fibonacci/extract_min` (422 if empty), `POST /api/v1/fibonacci/decrease_key` (body `{handle, value}`; 422 bad/dead handle / key-increase), `GET /api/v1/fibonacci/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/fibonacci/reset`.

Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 154D: `tests/test_fibonacci_heap.py` (35) + `tests/test_fibonacci_heap_web.py` (17) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against a brute `{handle‚Üívalue}` dict** (10 000 mixed ops, using `find_min_handle` to stay exactly in sync) + full-drain == `sorted` (60 trials) + 5 000-element drain + a cascading-cut stress; decrease-to-new-min / decrease-root, duplicates, floats/negatives, insertion-order independence; validation (empty pop, non-num, bad/dead/non-int handle, key-increase, bool) + `FibonacciHeapError.detail`; reset; determinism; 4-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `prquadtree`).

**Phase 155 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 327 test modules green. Sovereign AVL Tree (Adelson-Velsky & Landis, 1962) ‚ÄĒ a **height-balanced comparison-ordered set** with *guaranteed* `O(log n)` `insert` / `delete` / `contains` / `successor` / `predecessor` / `min` / `max`, kept balanced by tracking each node's subtree height and applying single/double rotations whenever a node's balance factor leaves `{‚ąí1, 0, +1}`. Unlike the platform's other search trees it is *strictly* balanced on every update ‚ÄĒ distinct from the amortized Splay Tree/P133, the randomized Treap, the RMQ Cartesian Tree/P145, and the integer-universe vEB/P152 (AVL orders *any* mutually-comparable keys: ints, floats, strings; duplicates ignored; `successor`/`predecessor` work for keys not present). Supports `insert(key)`, `delete(key)`, `contains(key)`, `successor(key)`, `predecessor(key)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `in_order()`, `height()`, `size`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a sorted reference set matched `in_order == sorted`, `contains`, `successor`/`predecessor` (1 840 point checks) and min/max across 40 random insert/delete trials, with the AVL balance invariant (`|bf| ‚Č§ 1` and stored heights correct at every node) re-checked after each trial**; the height stayed `‚Č§ 1.44 log‚āā(n+2)` even under 5 000 *sorted* and *reverse-sorted* insertions (the naive-BST worst case), and sorted-delete-half, string/float keys, and duplicate-ignoring all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/avl`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; recursion depth structurally bounded at `‚Č§ 1.44 log‚āā n` (the AVL height bound ‚ÄĒ never degenerate). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/avl_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 155A: `pradyos/core/avl_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `AVLTreeError(detail)`; `AVLTree()` with `insert(key)` ‚Üí bool, `delete(key)` ‚Üí bool, `contains(key)`, `successor(key)`, `predecessor(key)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `in_order()`, `height()`, `reset()`, `is_empty()`, `size` / `len()` + `stats()`. Keys must be `int`/`float`/`str` (no bool/None); mixed-type comparisons raise `AVLTreeError`. Generic balance-factor `_rebalance` (single/double rotations) shared by insert and delete; iterative `in_order`.
- ‚úÖ 155B: `pradyos/web/avl_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_avl_routes(app, avl_tree=None)` mounts 7 routes: `POST /api/v1/avl/insert` (body `{key}`, type-preserving), `POST /api/v1/avl/delete` (body `{key}`), `GET /api/v1/avl/contains` (`?key=`), `GET /api/v1/avl/successor` (may be null), `GET /api/v1/avl/predecessor` (may be null), `GET /api/v1/avl/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/avl/reset`. Non-orderable / mixed-type ‚Üí 422.

Existing routes untouched.

**Phase 156 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 329 test modules green. Sovereign B-Tree (Bayer & McCreight, 1972) ‚ÄĒ a **multiway balanced search tree** of minimum degree `t` where every node holds between `t‚ąí1` and `2t‚ąí1` keys and all leaves sit at the same depth, the canonical database/filesystem index. It keeps perfect balance with `O(t log‚āú n)` `insert` / `delete` / `search`, splitting a full child *proactively* on the way down to insert and **borrowing from a sibling or merging** to keep every node at least half-full before descending on delete ‚ÄĒ a fundamentally different *shape* from every *binary* tree on the platform (AVL/P155, Splay/P133, Treap, Cartesian/P145). It is an ordered set (duplicates ignored) over any mutually-comparable keys. Supports `insert(key)`, `delete(key)`, `contains(key)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `in_order()`, `height()`, `min_degree`, `size`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a sorted reference set matched `in_order == sorted` and `contains`, with the full B-tree structural invariant ‚ÄĒ every non-root node holds `t‚ąí1..2t‚ąí1` keys, internal child-count = key-count + 1, all leaves at one depth, cross-child key ordering ‚ÄĒ re-checked after *every* op across minimum degrees `t = 2, 3, 5`** (plus a 2 000-op `t=2` 2-3-4-tree churn); 5 000-key sorted and reverse-sorted insertion stay balanced (`height ‚Č§ 20` for 10 000 keys), sorted-delete-half, delete-all-to-empty (root collapses to a leaf), internal-node deletes, string/float keys all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/btree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; recursion depth structurally bounded at `O(log‚āú n)` (all leaves equidistant ‚ÄĒ never degenerate). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/b_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 156A: `pradyos/core/b_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `BTreeError(detail)`; `BTree(min_degree=3)` with `insert(key)` ‚Üí bool, `delete(key)` ‚Üí bool, `contains(key)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `in_order()`, `height()`, `reset()`, `is_empty()`, `size` / `len()` / `min_degree` + `stats()`. `min_degree ‚Č• 2`; keys `int`/`float`/`str` (no bool/None); mixed-type comparisons raise `BTreeError`. Proactive `_split_child` on insert; `_ensure_child` (borrow/merge) + predecessor/successor swap on delete; root collapses when emptied.
- ‚úÖ 156B: `pradyos/web/b_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_btree_routes(app, b_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/btree/insert` (body `{key}`, type-preserving), `POST /api/v1/btree/delete` (body `{key}`), `GET /api/v1/btree/contains` (`?key=`), `GET /api/v1/btree/keys` (in-order), `GET /api/v1/btree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/btree/reset`. Non-orderable / mixed-type ‚Üí 422.
- ‚úÖ 156C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase156.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `b_tree` param, and a single `register_btree_routes(app, b_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 156D: `tests/test_b_tree.py` (35) + `tests/test_b_tree_web.py` (16) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against a sorted reference set** with the full structural invariant re-checked each op across `t = 2, 3, 5` + a 2-3-4 churn; sorted/reverse 5 000-insert balance, sorted-delete-half, delete-all, internal-node deletes, height bound, string & float keys; validation (`min_degree=1`, None, bool, unorderable, mixed-type) + `BTreeError.detail`; reset; determinism; 4-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `avl`).

**Phase 157 ‚ÄĒ Complete.** All 331 test modules green. Sovereign Range Tree (Bentley, 1979) ‚ÄĒ a **2-D orthogonal range-search structure** answering "which points lie in an axis-aligned rectangle" in `O(log¬≤n + k)` (report) / `O(log¬≤n)` (count). It is a balanced BST keyed on `x` where every node additionally stores its subtree's points **pre-sorted by `y`**; a query descends to the `O(log n)` *canonical* `x`-nodes whose x-range is fully contained in `[x_min, x_max]` and binary-searches each node's `y`-array for the `y`-interval. This is the *textbook layered* orthogonal-range structure ‚ÄĒ distinct from the space-subdividing PR Quadtree/P153 and the median-split KD-Tree/P139, which answer the same query with different shapes and without the `O(log¬≤n)` worst-case guarantee. It is **static** (built once from a point set); each node's y-array is produced by an `O(n)` merge of its children's, so build is `O(n log n)`. Supports `build(points)`, `range_query(x_min, y_min, x_max, y_max)`, `range_count(...)`, `height()`, `size`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute point filter matched `range_query` and `range_count` over 400 random rectangle queries across 40 point clouds** plus a 3 000-point differential and a 50√ó50 grid sweep; full-bounds-all, duplicate points (multiset), inclusive boundaries, negative/float coords, and collinear same-x / same-y point sets (which stress the canonical decomposition over x-duplicates) all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/rangetree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; balanced-BST build ‚Üí recursion depth structurally bounded at `O(log n)` (midpoint split ‚ÄĒ never degenerate); queries iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/range_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ‚úÖ 157A: `pradyos/core/range_tree.py` ‚ÄĒ `RangeTreeError(detail)`; `RangeTree(points=None)` with `build(points)`, `range_query(x_min, y_min, x_max, y_max)` ‚Üí sorted `(x, y)` list, `range_count(...)` ‚Üí int, `height()`, `reset()`, `is_empty()`, `size` / `len()` + `stats()`. Points must be `(x, y)` number pairs; query rectangle numbers with `x_min ‚Č§ x_max`, `y_min ‚Č§ y_max` ‚ÄĒ violations raise `RangeTreeError`. Balanced x-BST built from the x-sorted array; per-node y-arrays via merge; iterative stack query selecting canonical x-nodes + `bisect` over y.
- ‚úÖ 157B: `pradyos/web/range_tree_web.py` ‚ÄĒ `register_rangetree_routes(app, range_tree=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/rangetree/build` (body `{points}`), `GET /api/v1/rangetree/range_query` (`?x_min=&y_min=&x_max=&y_max=`), `GET /api/v1/rangetree/range_count` (same query), `GET /api/v1/rangetree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/rangetree/reset`. Malformed points / inverted rect ‚Üí 422.
- ‚úÖ 157C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase157.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `range_tree` param, and a single `register_rangetree_routes(app, range_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ‚úÖ 157D: `tests/test_range_tree.py` (33) + `tests/test_range_tree_web.py` (18) ‚ÄĒ **a differential test against a brute point filter** for `range_query`/`range_count` (400 queries / 40 clouds + a 3 000-point set + a 50√ó50 grid); duplicates, boundaries, negatives/floats, collinear same-x / same-y, thin strips; validation (bad point, non-num, non-iterable, inverted rect) + `RangeTreeError.detail`; rebuild / reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `btree`).
